#93 cloud93 — Learn about Shemittah — the seventh year when the land of Israel rests — and wha

EN Learn about Shemittah \u2014 the seventh year when the land of Israel rests \u2014 and what this actually means for Jews living in Israel today! \ud83c\udf3e Every seven years, the Torah commands that the land of Israel must rest: no plowing, planting, pruning, or commercial harvesting. Generally you're only allowed to do basic things to keep plants alive but not to improve them. Produce that grows on its own during Shemittah has 'kedushat shevi'it' (seventh-year sanctity) and can't be sold normally. The challenge: how does a country of millions survive without farming for a year? Two main halachic solutions are used today in Israel: (1) 'Heter Mechira' \u2014 a legal sale of Israeli farmland to a non-Jew for the year, so technically a non-Jew 'owns' the land during Shemittah and can farm it. The Chief Rabbinate permits this; many orthodox authorities do not. (2) 'Otzar Beit Din' \u2014 a rabbinical court takes formal ownership of the crops and distributes them, charging only for labor costs, not for the produce itself. Products with Otzar Beit Din certification need to be treated with Shemittah sanctity in your home (eaten and not wasted or destroyed). If the produce rots on its own that's fine, but you can't add it to the garbage and thus intentionally make it inedible. Many people use special \"Shemittah bins\" that let the food decompose naturally if they're not going to eat it. Authorities debate whether it's a positive mitzvah to enjoy holy Shemittah fruit. Many say it is! Learn more.
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05e9\u05de\u05d9\u05d8\u05d4 \u2014 \u05d4\u05e9\u05e0\u05d4 \u05d4\u05e9\u05d1\u05d9\u05e2\u05d9\u05ea \u05e9\u05d1\u05d4 \u05d4\u05d0\u05d3\u05de\u05d4 \u05d1\u05d0\u05e8\u05e5 \u05d9\u05e9\u05e8\u05d0\u05dc \u05e0\u05d7\u05d4 \u2014 \u05d5\u05de\u05d4 \u05d6\u05d4 \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d9\u05d4\u05d5\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05d9\u05e9\u05e8\u05d0\u05dc \u05d4\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd! \ud83c\udf3e \u05db\u05dc \u05e9\u05d1\u05e2 \u05e9\u05e0\u05d9\u05dd \u05d4\u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4 \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05d4: \u05d0\u05d9\u05df \u05d7\u05e8\u05d9\u05e9\u05d4, \u05d6\u05e8\u05d9\u05e2\u05d4, \u05d2\u05d9\u05d6\u05d5\u05dd \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e7\u05e6\u05d9\u05e8 \u05de\u05e1\u05d7\u05e8\u05d9. \u05de\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8 \u05e8\u05e7 \u05dc\u05e9\u05de\u05d5\u05e8 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d4\u05e6\u05de\u05d7\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd, \u05dc\u05d0 \u05dc\u05e9\u05e4\u05e8 \u05d0\u05d5\u05ea\u05dd. \u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05e2\u05dd \u05e7\u05d3\u05d5\u05e9\u05ea \u05e9\u05d1\u05d9\u05e2\u05d9\u05ea \u05dc\u05d0 \u05e0\u05de\u05db\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05db\u05e8\u05d2\u05d9\u05dc. \u05d0\u05d9\u05da \u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05e0\u05d4 \u05e9\u05dc \u05de\u05d9\u05dc\u05d9\u05d5\u05e0\u05d9\u05dd \u05e9\u05d5\u05e8\u05d3\u05ea \u05e9\u05e0\u05d4 \u05d1\u05dc\u05d9 \u05d7\u05e7\u05dc\u05d0\u05d5\u05ea? (1) \u05d4\u05d9\u05ea\u05e8 \u05de\u05db\u05d9\u05e8\u05d4 \u2014 \u05de\u05db\u05d9\u05e8\u05ea \u05d4\u05d0\u05d3\u05de\u05d4 \u05dc\u05d2\u05d5\u05d9 \u05dc\u05e9\u05e0\u05d4 (\u05e8\u05d1\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05e0\u05d4; \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd \u05d7\u05d5\u05dc\u05e7\u05d9\u05dd). (2) \u05d0\u05d5\u05e6\u05e8 \u05d1\u05d9\u05ea \u05d3\u05d9\u05df \u2014 \u05d1\u05d9\u05ea \u05d3\u05d9\u05df \u05de\u05d7\u05d6\u05d9\u05e7 \u05d1\u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05d5\u05de\u05d7\u05dc\u05e7, \u05e8\u05e7 \u05e2\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea \u05e2\u05d1\u05d5\u05d3\u05d4. \u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05d0\u05d5\u05e6\u05e8 \u05d1\u05d9\u05ea \u05d3\u05d9\u05df \u2014 \u05e7\u05d3\u05d5\u05e9\u05ea \u05e9\u05d1\u05d9\u05e2\u05d9\u05ea, \u05dc\u05d0 \u05dc\u05d6\u05e8\u05d5\u05e7 \u05d1\u05de\u05d5\u05d3\u05e2. \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd \u05de\u05e9\u05ea\u05de\u05e9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\"\u05e4\u05d7 \u05e9\u05de\u05d9\u05d8\u05d4\" \u05dc\u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05e7 \u05d8\u05d1\u05e2\u05d9. \u05d9\u05e9 \u05de\u05d7\u05dc\u05d5\u05e7\u05ea \u05d0\u05dd \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05d4 \u05dc\u05d9\u05d4\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05de\u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05de\u05d9\u05d8\u05d4 \u2014 \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05db\u05df! \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d3.
ES \u00a1Conoce el Shemit\u00e1 \u2014 el s\u00e9ptimo a\u00f1o en que la tierra de Israel descansa \u2014 y qu\u00e9 significa esto en realidad para los jud\u00edos que viven en Israel hoy! \ud83c\udf3e Cada siete a\u00f1os, la Tor\u00e1 ordena que la tierra de Israel debe descansar: sin arar, plantar, podar ni cosechar comercialmente. Generalmente solo se permiten cosas b\u00e1sicas para mantener las plantas vivas, pero no para mejorarlas. Los productos que crecen por s\u00ed solos durante el Shemit\u00e1 tienen \"kedushat shevi'it\" (santidad del s\u00e9ptimo a\u00f1o) y no pueden venderse normalmente. El desaf\u00edo: \u00bfc\u00f3mo sobrevive un pa\u00eds de millones sin agricultura durante un a\u00f1o? Hoy en Israel se usan dos soluciones hal\u00e1jicas principales: (1) \"Heter Mejir\u00e1\" \u2014 una venta legal de tierras agr\u00edcolas israel\u00edes a un no jud\u00edo por el a\u00f1o, de modo que t\u00e9cnicamente un no jud\u00edo \"posee\" la tierra durante el Shemit\u00e1 y puede cultivarla. El Rabbinate Chief lo permite; muchas autoridades ortodoxas no. (2) \"Otzar Beit Din\" \u2014 un tribunal rab\u00ednico toma posesi\u00f3n formal de los cultivos y los distribuye, cobrando solo costos de mano de obra, no el producto en s\u00ed. Los productos con certificaci\u00f3n Otzar Beit Din deben tratarse con santidad de Shemit\u00e1 en tu hogar (comerse y no desperdiciarse ni destruirse). Si el producto se pudre por s\u00ed solo, est\u00e1 bien, pero no puedes tirarlo a la basura e intencionalmente hacerlo inedible. Muchas personas usan \"contenedores de Shemit\u00e1\" especiales que permiten que la comida se descomponga naturalmente si no van a comerla. Las autoridades debaten si es una mitzv\u00e1 positiva disfrutar de la fruta sagrada del Shemit\u00e1. \u00a1Muchos dicen que s\u00ed! Aprende m\u00e1s.
FR Apprenez la Shemittah \u2014 la septi\u00e8me ann\u00e9e o\u00f9 la terre d'Isra\u00ebl se repose \u2014 et ce que cela signifie concr\u00e8tement pour les Juifs vivant en Isra\u00ebl aujourd'hui ! \ud83c\udf3e Tous les sept ans, la Torah commande que la terre d'Isra\u00ebl se repose : pas de labour, plantation, taille ou r\u00e9colte commerciale. En g\u00e9n\u00e9ral, vous n'\u00eates autoris\u00e9 qu'\u00e0 faire des choses basiques pour maintenir les plantes en vie, mais pas pour les am\u00e9liorer. Les produits qui poussent d'eux-m\u00eames pendant la Shemittah ont une \u00ab kedouchat shevi'it \u00bb (saintet\u00e9 de la septi\u00e8me ann\u00e9e) et ne peuvent pas \u00eatre vendus normalement. Le d\u00e9fi : comment un pays de millions de personnes survit-il sans agriculture pendant un an ? Deux principales solutions halachiques sont utilis\u00e9es aujourd'hui en Isra\u00ebl : (1) \u00ab Heter Mechira \u00bb \u2014 une vente l\u00e9gale de terres agricoles isra\u00e9liennes \u00e0 un non-Juif pour l'ann\u00e9e, de sorte qu'un non-Juif \u00ab poss\u00e8de \u00bb techniquement la terre pendant la Shemittah et peut la cultiver. Le Grand Rabbinat l'autorise ; de nombreuses autorit\u00e9s orthodoxes ne le font pas. (2) \u00ab Otzar Beit Din \u00bb \u2014 un tribunal rabbinique prend formellement possession des r\u00e9coltes et les distribue, en ne facturant que les co\u00fbts de main-d'\u0153uvre, pas le produit lui-m\u00eame. Les produits avec certification Otzar Beit Din doivent \u00eatre trait\u00e9s avec la saintet\u00e9 de la Shemittah chez vous (consomm\u00e9s et non gaspill\u00e9s ou d\u00e9truits). Si le produit pourrit de lui-m\u00eame, c'est acceptable, mais vous ne pouvez pas le jeter aux ordures et le rendre ainsi volontairement non comestible. Beaucoup de gens utilisent des \u00ab bacs Shemittah \u00bb sp\u00e9ciaux qui laissent la nourriture se d\u00e9composer naturellement s'ils ne vont pas la manger. Les autorit\u00e9s d\u00e9battent de savoir s'il s'agit d'une mitzvah positive de profiter des fruits saints de la Shemittah. Beaucoup le pensent ! Apprenez-en plus.

#94 cloud94 — Learn about the Tithe-to-Table system that turns every Israeli snack into a holy

EN Learn about the Tithe-to-Table system that turns every Israeli snack into a holy mission! \ud83e\uddfa In the land of Israel, your fruits and veggies aren't just food\u2014they are part of a massive spiritual cycle. Before you can take a single bite, you have to de-classify the produce from its restricted state called Tevel by separating several specific portions. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f The holy order of operations starts with Terumah Gedolah, a portion of the crop originally given to the Kohanim. Because it is super holy, only Kohanim in a state of purity could eat it (no one is in a state of purity today so we don't eat this nowadays). \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f Then comes Maaser Rishon, where ten percent of what remains goes to the Levites. Next is the swing tithe called Maaser Sheni or Ani. In years one, two, four, and five of the Shemittah cycle, you would take another ten percent to Jerusalem for a holy feast! But in years three and six, that portion becomes Maaser Ani and goes straight to the poor. \ud83c\udf4e\ud83e\udd1d Even today, if you are shopping in an Israeli shuk, you might encounter Tevel, which is food that hasn't been processed yet. Modern halacha keeps the tradition alive by separating small symbolic amounts. It is like a spiritual tax that reminds us that the land doesn't belong to us, it belongs to Hashem!
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05de\u05e2\u05e8\u05db\u05ea \u05d4\u05de\u05e2\u05e9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea! \ud83e\uddfa \u05dc\u05e4\u05e0\u05d9 \u05db\u05dc \u05e0\u05e9\u05d9\u05db\u05d4 \u05de\u05e4\u05e8\u05d9\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05ea\u05e8\u05d5\u05de\u05d4, \u05de\u05e2\u05e9\u05e8 \u05e8\u05d0\u05e9\u05d5\u05df, \u05de\u05e2\u05e9\u05e8 \u05e9\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d0\u05d5 \u05de\u05e2\u05e9\u05e8 \u05e2\u05e0\u05d9. \u05d6\u05d5 \u05de\u05e1 \u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9 \u05e9\u05de\u05d6\u05db\u05d9\u05e8: \u05d4\u05d0\u05d3\u05de\u05d4 \u05e9\u05d9\u05d9\u05db\u05ea \u05dc\u05d4'. \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d3!
ES \u00a1Conoce el sistema de Diezmo-a-la-Mesa que convierte cada snack israel\u00ed en una misi\u00f3n sagrada! \ud83e\uddfa En la tierra de Israel, tus frutas y verduras no son solo comida \u2014 son parte de un ciclo espiritual masivo. Antes de dar un solo bocado, debes desclasificar el producto de su estado restringido llamado Tevel separando varias porciones espec\u00edficas. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f El orden sagrado de operaciones comienza con Terum\u00e1 Gedol\u00e1, una porci\u00f3n del cultivo originalmente dada a los kohanim. Por ser super sagrada, solo los kohanim en estado de pureza pod\u00edan comerla (hoy nadie est\u00e1 en estado de pureza, as\u00ed que no comemos esto). \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f Luego viene Maaser Rishon, donde el diez por ciento de lo que queda va a los levitas. Despu\u00e9s est\u00e1 el diezmo alterno llamado Maaser Sheni o Ani. En los a\u00f1os uno, dos, cuatro y cinco del ciclo de Shemit\u00e1, tomabas otro diez por ciento a Jerusal\u00e9n para un banquete sagrado. Pero en los a\u00f1os tres y seis, esa porci\u00f3n se convierte en Maaser Ani y va directamente a los pobres. \ud83c\udf4e\ud83e\udd1d Incluso hoy, si compras en un shuk israel\u00ed, puedes encontrar Tevel, que es comida que a\u00fan no ha sido procesada. La halaj\u00e1 moderna mantiene viva la tradici\u00f3n separando peque\u00f1as cantidades simb\u00f3licas. Es como un impuesto espiritual que nos recuerda que la tierra no nos pertenece, \u00a1pertenece a Hashem!
FR Apprenez le syst\u00e8me Tithe-to-Table qui transforme chaque collation isra\u00e9lienne en mission sainte ! \ud83e\uddfa En terre d'Isra\u00ebl, vos fruits et l\u00e9gumes ne sont pas que de la nourriture \u2014 ils font partie d'un immense cycle spirituel. #95 cloud95 — Prepare for the ultimate harvest parade

EN Prepare for the ultimate harvest parade! \ud83c\udf47 Learn about Bikkurim, the first-fruit offering that was one of the most emotional and high-energy ceremonies in the entire Temple service. When a farmer saw the very first ripening fruits of the Seven Species\u2014wheat, barley, grapes, figs, pomegranates, olives, and dates\u2014he would tie a reed around them to mark them as holy. \ud83c\udf80 The journey to Jerusalem was a nationwide block party! \ud83e\udd73 Pilgrims traveled together in massive groups, and as they entered the city, the local artisans and leaders would stop their work to stand up and welcome them! \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f The streets filled with music from the flutes of the Levi'im as the parade headed toward the Temple Mount. The coolest part is the declaration the farmer made while holding his basket. He would recount the history of the Jewish people from the Exodus until that very moment of standing on his own land. \ud83d\udcdc Rich farmers brought their fruits in baskets of gold and silver, while the poor used simple wicker, but everyone\u2019s offering was cherished. While we can't bring these physical fruits today without the Temple, this ceremony represents the ultimate goal of living with gratitude and national unity. It\u2019s a beautiful preview of the celebrations we\u2019ll see again when the third Temple is built! \ud83c\udf8a\ud83c\udf4e.

Cuando un agricultor ve\u00eda las primeras frutas madurando de las Siete Especies \u2014 trigo, cebada, uvas, higos, granadas, aceitunas y d\u00e1tiles \u2014 ataba una ca\u00f1a alrededor de ellas para marcarlas como sagradas. \ud83c\udf80 El viaje a Jerusal\u00e9n era una fiesta callejera a nivel nacional. \ud83e\udd73 Los peregrinos viajaban juntos en grupos masivos, y al entrar en la ciudad, los artesanos y l\u00edderes locales dejaban su trabajo para ponerse de pie y darles la bienvenida. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f Las calles se llenaban de m\u00fasica de las flautas de los Levi'im mientras el desfile se dirig\u00eda hacia el Monte del Templo. #96 cloud96 — Learn about the mitzvah of Halvayat HaMeit, the sacred act of accompanying the d

EN Learn about the mitzvah of Halvayat HaMeit, the sacred act of accompanying the deceased to their final resting place! \ud83d\udcdc This is famously called chesed shel emet, or true kindness, because it is the purest form of giving where the recipient can never repay the favor. The Rambam explains that this is a full Torah obligation rooted in the commandment to love your neighbor as yourself! \ud83d\udc99 Even walking just a few steps with a coffin is considered a massive mitzvah that brings incredible honor to the departed soul. People often even interrupt their Torah study to join a funeral procession and pay their respects. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f This act of escorting the deceased shows that every single Jewish person is a vessel of holiness and deserves to be treated with dignity until the very end. Learn more!
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d4\u05dc\u05d5\u05d5\u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05de\u05d9\u05ea \u2014 \u05d7\u05e1\u05d3 \u05e9\u05dc \u05d0\u05de\u05ea! \ud83d\udcdc \u05d4\u05e8\u05de\u05d1\"\u05dd \u05de\u05e1\u05d1\u05d9\u05e8 \u05e9\u05d6\u05d5 \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05ea \u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4 \u05de\u05dc\u05d0\u05d4 \u05de\u05d0\u05d4\u05d1\u05ea \u05dc\u05e8\u05e2\u05da \u05db\u05de\u05d5\u05da. \u05d2\u05dd \u05db\u05de\u05d4 \u05e6\u05e2\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05e2\u05dd \u05d4\u05de\u05d9\u05ea \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05d4 \u05e2\u05e6\u05d5\u05de\u05d4. \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d3!
ES \u00a1Conoce la mitzv\u00e1 de Halvayat HaMeit, el acto sagrado de acompa\u00f1ar al difunto a su lugar de descanso final! \ud83d\udcdc Esto se conoce famosamente como j\u00e9sed shel emet, o bondad verdadera, porque es la forma m\u00e1s pura de dar donde el receptor nunca puede devolver el favor. El Rambam explica que es una obligaci\u00f3n completa de la Tor\u00e1 arraigada en el mandamiento de amar a tu pr\u00f3jimo como a ti mismo. \ud83d\udc99 Incluso caminar solo unos pasos con un ata\u00fad se considera una mitzv\u00e1 enorme que trae un honor incre\u00edble al alma del difunto. A menudo la gente incluso interrumpe su estudio de Tor\u00e1 para unirse a un cortejo f\u00fanebre y rendir homenaje. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f Este acto de escoltar al difunto muestra que cada persona jud\u00eda es un vaso de santidad y merece ser tratada con dignidad hasta el final. \u00a1Aprende m\u00e1s!
FR Apprenez la mitzvah de Halvayat HaMeit, l'acte sacr\u00e9 d'accompagner le d\u00e9funt jusqu'\u00e0 son dernier repos ! \ud83d\udcdc C'est ce qu'on appelle c\u00e9l\u00e8brement le chesed shel emet, ou la bont\u00e9 v\u00e9ritable, car c'est la forme la plus pure de don o\u00f9 le b\u00e9n\u00e9ficiaire ne peut jamais rendre la faveur. Le Rambam explique que c'est une obligation toranique compl\u00e8te enracin\u00e9e dans le commandement d'aimer ton prochain comme toi-m\u00eame ! \ud83d\udc99 M\u00eame marcher seulement quelques pas avec un cercueil est consid\u00e9r\u00e9 comme une mitzvah massive qui apporte un honneur incroyable \u00e0 l'\u00e2me du d\u00e9funt. Les gens interrompent souvent leur \u00e9tude de la Torah pour rejoindre une procession fun\u00e9raire et rendre hommage. \ud83c\udfdb\ufe0f Cet acte d'accompagnement du d\u00e9funt montre que chaque personne juive est un r\u00e9ceptacle de saintet\u00e9 et m\u00e9rite d'\u00eatre trait\u00e9e avec dignit\u00e9 jusqu'\u00e0 la toute fin. Apprenez-en plus !

#97 cloud97 — Learn about the prohibition of 'chukot ha'akum' — following non-Jewish customs —

EN Learn about the prohibition of 'chukot ha'akum' \u2014 following non-Jewish customs \u2014 and how nuanced the actual halacha is! \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f The Torah says 'You shall not follow the customs of the nation' (Leviticus 18:3). The Rambam and the Shulchan Aruch codify this as a prohibition against adopting practices associated with non-Jewish religions or that originated as pagan customs. The Shulchan Aruch (Yoreh Deah 178) rules: a Jewish person may not wear distinctive non-Jewish clothing if its purpose is to imitate them, especially for religious or idolatrous reasons. What is NOT prohibited: things that have become universally adopted for practical reasons (e.g., wearing a suit and tie \u2014 not pagan, just practical business clothing). The prohibition targets customs that are 'chukat hagoy' \u2014 practices specifically identified with non-Jewish religious tradition or that have no logical basis except as their tradition. Important: this prohibition has nothing to do with disrespecting non-Jews \u2014 it's about maintaining a distinct Jewish identity and avoiding spiritual confusion!
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d0\u05d9\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05d7\u05d5\u05e7\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05d5\u05ea! \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f \u05d4\u05e8\u05de\u05d1\"\u05dd \u05d5\u05e9\u05d5\u05dc\u05d7\u05df \u05e2\u05e8\u05d5\u05da \u05e7\u05d5\u05d1\u05e2\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05d9\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d4\u05e2\u05ea\u05d9\u05e7 \u05de\u05e0\u05d4\u05d2\u05d9 \u05d3\u05ea \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d1\u05d5\u05d3\u05d4 \u05d6\u05e8\u05d4. \u05de\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8: \u05d3\u05d1\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05e9\u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05e9\u05d8\u05d5 \u05dc\u05de\u05d8\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05e2\u05e9\u05d9\u05ea. \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d3!
ES \u00a1Conoce la prohibici\u00f3n de \"jukot ha'akum\" \u2014 seguir costumbres no jud\u00edas \u2014 y lo matizado que es en realidad la halaj\u00e1! \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f La Tor\u00e1 dice: \"No seguir\u00e9is las costumbres de la naci\u00f3n\" (Lev\u00edtico 18:3). El Rambam y el Shulj\u00e1n Aruj lo codifican como una prohibici\u00f3n contra adoptar pr\u00e1cticas asociadas con religiones no jud\u00edas o que se originaron como costumbres paganas. El Shulj\u00e1n Aruj (Yoreh Deah 178) establece: un jud\u00edo no puede usar ropa distintiva no jud\u00eda si su prop\u00f3sito es imitarlos, especialmente por razones religiosas o idol\u00e1tricas. Lo que NO est\u00e1 prohibido: cosas adoptadas universalmente por razones pr\u00e1cticas (por ejemplo, usar traje y corbata \u2014 no es pagano, solo ropa de negocios pr\u00e1ctica). La prohibici\u00f3n apunta a costumbres que son \"jukat hagoy\" \u2014 pr\u00e1cticas espec\u00edficamente identificadas con la tradici\u00f3n religiosa no jud\u00eda o que no tienen base l\u00f3gica excepto como su tradici\u00f3n. Importante: esta prohibici\u00f3n no tiene nada que ver con faltarle al respeto a los no jud\u00edos \u2014 se trata de mantener una identidad jud\u00eda distinta y evitar confusi\u00f3n espiritual.
FR Apprenez l'interdiction des \u00ab 'houkot ha'akum \u00bb \u2014 suivre les coutumes non juives \u2014 et \u00e0 quel point la halacha r\u00e9elle est nuanc\u00e9e ! \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f La Torah dit : \u00ab Vous ne suivrez pas les coutumes de la nation \u00bb (L\u00e9vitique 18:3). Le Rambam et le Choulhan Aroukh codifient cela comme une interdiction d'adopter des pratiques associ\u00e9es aux religions non juives ou ayant pour origine des coutumes pa\u00efennes. Le Choulhan Aroukh (Yoreh Deah 178) statue : une personne juive ne peut pas porter de v\u00eatements distinctifs non juifs si le but est de les imiter, surtout pour des raisons religieuses ou idol\u00e2tres. Ce qui N'est PAS interdit : les choses universellement adopt\u00e9es pour des raisons pratiques (par exemple, porter un costume-cravate \u2014 pas pa\u00efen, juste un v\u00eatement professionnel pratique). L'interdiction vise les coutumes qui sont \u00ab 'houkat hagoy \u00bb \u2014 des pratiques sp\u00e9cifiquement identifi\u00e9es \u00e0 la tradition religieuse non juive ou qui n'ont aucune base logique sauf en tant que leur tradition. Important : cette interdiction n'a rien \u00e0 voir avec le manque de respect envers les non-Juifs \u2014 il s'agit de maintenir une identit\u00e9 juive distincte et d'\u00e9viter la confusion spirituelle !

EN Learn about the Rambam's specific, practical description of what the Messianic era will actually look like \u2014 you might be surprised how down-to-earth it is! \ud83c\udf0d The Rambam's famous ruling (Hilchot Melachim 11-12): 'The Messianic King will arise and restore the monarchy of David to its former glory... He will rebuild the Temple and gather all of Israel.' But then the Rambam adds something remarkable: 'Do not think the world will depart from its normal course in the Messianic era... A wolf will not dwell with the lamb \u2014 this is a metaphor for Israel dwelling peacefully among the nations.' The Rambam explicitly rules that the Messianic era will be a NATURAL time, not supernatural. Trees will still need to be planted, the sun will rise and set normally. The difference: Israel will be free from foreign oppression, and will be able to devote themselves to Torah study without distraction. 'In that time there will be no hunger, no war, no jealousy, no conflict \u2014 for good things will be plentiful, and all delicacies available like dust.' And the ultimate purpose: 'The sages and prophets did not yearn for the Messianic era in order to rule the world or to eat, drink, and be merry \u2014 but in order to be free to study Torah and wisdom, with no one oppressing them.' There are other rabbis who disagree and hold that the world will not be so normal, and instead that it will be a time of open miracles. Which one do you think would be better?

#99 cloud99 — Learn the specific conditions under which speaking negatively about someone is P

EN Learn the specific conditions under which speaking negatively about someone is PERMITTED \u2014 because lashon hara has important exceptions! \ud83d\udc44 The Chofetz Chaim (Rabbi Yisrael Meir Kagan, the definitive authority on lashon hara law) rules that negative speech is permitted \u2014 and sometimes obligatory \u2014 when ALL seven conditions are met: (1) The information must be TRUE \u2014 you verified it yourself. (2) It must be NECESSARY \u2014 there's a genuine toelet (constructive purpose), not just sharing information. (3) You must first try to solve the problem by speaking directly to the person who wronged someone, before reporting to a third party. (4) The information shared must be PROPORTIONATE to the actual harm \u2014 don't exaggerate. (5) Your intention must be purely for the benefit, not for personal satisfaction or revenge. (6) The damage caused by revealing it must not be GREATER than the damage prevented. (7) There must be no other way to accomplish the goal. The classic permitted case: warning someone that their potential business partner is a known fraudster. You MUST tell them \u2014 withholding the information would cause harm. So the prohibition of lashon hara is not 'never say anything negative' \u2014 it's 'never say anything negative without a real, valid purpose.' Learn more!
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05de\u05ea\u05d9 \u05de\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u05e8\u05e2 \u2014 \u05dc\u05e9\u05d5\u05df \u05d4\u05e8\u05e2 \u05d9\u05e9 \u05d7\u05e8\u05d9\u05d2\u05d9\u05dd! \ud83d\udc44 \u05d4\u05d7\u05e4\u05e5 \u05d7\u05d9\u05dd \u05e7\u05d5\u05d1\u05e2 \u05e9\u05d1\u05e2 \u05ea\u05e0\u05d0\u05d9\u05dd \u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd: \u05d0\u05de\u05ea, \u05e6\u05d5\u05e8\u05da, \u05e0\u05d9\u05e1\u05d9\u05d5\u05df, \u05e4\u05e8\u05d5\u05e4\u05d5\u05e8\u05e6\u05d9\u05d4, \u05db\u05d5\u05d5\u05e0\u05d4 \u05d8\u05d4\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4, \u05d4\u05e4\u05d7\u05ea\u05ea \u05e0\u05d6\u05e7, \u05d0\u05d9\u05df \u05d3\u05e8\u05da \u05d0\u05d7\u05e8\u05ea. \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d3!
ES \u00a1Aprende las condiciones espec\u00edficas bajo las cuales hablar negativamente de alguien est\u00e1 PERMITIDO \u2014 porque el lashon har\u00e1 tiene excepciones importantes! \ud83d\udc44 El Jafetz Jaim (rab\u00ed Yisrael Meir Kagan, la autoridad definitiva en leyes de lashon har\u00e1) establece que el habla negativa est\u00e1 permitida \u2014 y a veces es obligatoria \u2014 cuando se cumplen TODAS las siete condiciones: (1) La informaci\u00f3n debe ser VERDADERA \u2014 la verificaste t\u00fa mismo. (2) Debe ser NECESARIA \u2014 hay un toelet (prop\u00f3sito constructivo) genuino, no solo compartir informaci\u00f3n. (3) Primero debes intentar resolver el problema hablando directamente con la persona que perjudic\u00f3 a alguien, antes de informar a un tercero. (4) La informaci\u00f3n compartida debe ser PROPORCIONAL al da\u00f1o real \u2014 no exageres. (5) Tu intenci\u00f3n debe ser puramente para el beneficio, no para satisfacci\u00f3n personal o venganza. (6) El da\u00f1o causado por revelarlo no debe ser MAYOR que el da\u00f1o prevenido. (7) No debe haber otra forma de lograr el objetivo. El caso cl\u00e1sico permitido: advertir a alguien que su posible socio comercial es un estafador conocido. DEBES dec\u00edrselo \u2014 retener la informaci\u00f3n causar\u00eda da\u00f1o. As\u00ed que la prohibici\u00f3n de lashon har\u00e1 no es \"nunca digas nada negativo\" \u2014 es \"nunca digas nada negativo sin un prop\u00f3sito real y v\u00e1lido\". \u00a1Aprende m\u00e1s!
FR Apprenez les conditions pr\u00e9cises dans lesquelles parler n\u00e9gativement de quelqu'un est PERMIS \u2014 car le lashon hara a d'importantes exceptions ! \ud83d\udc44 Le Hafets 'Ha\u00efm (Rabbi Yisrael Meir Kagan, l'autorit\u00e9 d\u00e9finitive sur la loi du lashon hara) statue que la parole n\u00e9gative est permise \u2014 et parfois obligatoire \u2014 lorsque les SEPT conditions sont remplies : (1) L'information doit \u00eatre VRAIE \u2014 vous l'avez v\u00e9rifi\u00e9e vous-m\u00eame. (2) Elle doit \u00eatre N\u00c9CESSAIRE \u2014 il y a un toelet (but constructif) authentique, pas seulement le partage d'informations. (3) Vous devez d'abord essayer de r\u00e9soudre le probl\u00e8me en parlant directement \u00e0 la personne qui a l\u00e9s\u00e9 quelqu'un, avant de le signaler \u00e0 un tiers. (4) L'information partag\u00e9e doit \u00eatre PROPORTIONN\u00c9E au pr\u00e9judice r\u00e9el \u2014 ne pas exag\u00e9rer. (5) Votre intention doit \u00eatre purement au b\u00e9n\u00e9fice, pas pour satisfaction personnelle ou vengeance. (6) Le dommage caus\u00e9 par la r\u00e9v\u00e9lation ne doit pas \u00eatre PLUS GRAND que le dommage \u00e9vit\u00e9. (7) Il ne doit pas y avoir d'autre moyen d'atteindre l'objectif. Le cas classique permis : avertir quelqu'un que son futur partenaire commercial est un escroc connu. Vous DEVEZ le lui dire \u2014 retenir l'information causerait un pr\u00e9judice. L'interdiction du lashon hara n'est donc pas \u00ab ne jamais rien dire de n\u00e9gatif \u00bb \u2014 c'est \u00ab ne jamais rien dire de n\u00e9gatif sans un but r\u00e9el et valable \u00bb. #100 cloud100 — Learn about the prohibition of receiving lashon hara — which is equally serious

EN Learn about the prohibition of receiving lashon hara \u2014 which is equally serious to speaking it, and which is actually harder to avoid! \ud83e\udd10 The Chofetz Chaim rules: it is forbidden to LISTEN to lashon hara and believe it. More specifically, it's forbidden to: (1) Listen attentively and encourage the speaker to continue; (2) Enjoy hearing the negative information; (3) Believe what you've heard as established fact. The Talmud says a person who listens to lashon hara is actually worse than the speaker, because the speaker can repent by telling the person he spoke to that he made it up \u2014 but the listener has already received the information into his mind and the damage to his perception is done. Practical implications: If someone starts telling you something negative about a third party and you're stuck in the conversation \u2014 you have two levels of obligation: (a) Try to redirect or exit. (b) If stuck, consciously decide NOT to believe what you're hearing. You can listen without believing. The Chofetz Chaim calls this 'hearing without accepting.' One key insight: we are commanded NOT to believe lashon hara about another Jew \u2014 even if we can't immediately disprove it. We must maintain the assumption of innocence. This is extremely counterintuitive to modern ears, but it's actual halacha. Source: Chofetz Chaim, Hilchot Rechilut; Talmud, Niddah 61a.
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d0\u05d9\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05dc\u05e7\u05d1\u05dc \u05dc\u05e9\u05d5\u05df \u05d4\u05e8\u05e2! \ud83e\udd10 \u05d4\u05d7\u05e4\u05e5 \u05d7\u05d9\u05dd \u05e7\u05d5\u05d1\u05e2: \u05d0\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d4\u05d0\u05de\u05d9\u05df \u05d5\u05dc\u05d4\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05de\u05e9\u05de\u05d9\u05e2\u05ea \u05d4\u05d3\u05d1\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd. \u05d4\u05ea\u05dc\u05de\u05d5\u05d3 \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8 \u05e9\u05d4\u05e9\u05d5\u05de\u05e2 \u05d2\u05e8\u05d5\u05e2 \u05de\u05d4\u05de\u05d3\u05d1\u05e8. \u05e9\u05d5\u05de\u05e2\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05dc\u05d9 \u05dc\u05d4\u05d0\u05de\u05d9\u05df. \u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05e8: \u05d4\u05d7\u05e4\u05e5 \u05d7\u05d9\u05dd, \u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d5\u05ea \u05e8\u05db\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea; \u05d4\u05ea\u05dc\u05de\u05d5\u05d3, \u05e0\u05d3\u05d4 \u05e1\"\u05d0.
ES \u00a1Conoce la prohibici\u00f3n de recibir lashon har\u00e1 \u2014 que es igual de seria que hablarlo, \u00a1y que en realidad es m\u00e1s dif\u00edcil de evitar! \ud83e\udd10 El Jafetz Jaim establece: est\u00e1 prohibido ESCUCHAR lashon har\u00e1 y creerlo. M\u00e1s espec\u00edficamente, est\u00e1 prohibido: (1) Escuchar atentamente y animar al hablante a continuar; (2) Disfrutar escuchar la informaci\u00f3n negativa; (3) Creer lo que has o\u00eddo como hecho establecido. El Talmud dice que quien escucha lashon har\u00e1 es en realidad peor que quien habla, porque el hablante puede arrepentirse dici\u00e9ndole a la persona de quien habl\u00f3 que lo invent\u00f3 \u2014 pero el oyente ya recibi\u00f3 la informaci\u00f3n en su mente y el da\u00f1o a su percepci\u00f3n est\u00e1 hecho. Implicaciones pr\u00e1cticas: si alguien empieza a contarte algo negativo sobre un tercero y est\u00e1s atrapado en la conversaci\u00f3n, tienes dos niveles de obligaci\u00f3n: (a) Intentar redirigir o salir. (b) Si est\u00e1s atrapado, decidir conscientemente NO creer lo que escuchas. Puedes escuchar sin creer. El Jafetz Jaim llama a esto \"escuchar sin aceptar\". Una idea clave: estamos mandados a NO creer lashon har\u00e1 sobre otro jud\u00edo \u2014 aunque no podamos desmentirlo de inmediato. Debemos mantener la presunci\u00f3n de inocencia. Esto es extremadamente contraintuitivo para los o\u00eddos modernos, pero es halaj\u00e1 real. Fuente: Jafetz Jaim, Hilchot Rechilut; Talmud, Niddah 61a.
FR Apprenez l'interdiction de recevoir du lashon hara \u2014 qui est tout aussi grave que de le prononcer, et qui est en r\u00e9alit\u00e9 plus difficile \u00e0 \u00e9viter ! \ud83e\udd10 Le Hafets 'Ha\u00efm statue : il est interdit d'\u00c9COUTER le lashon hara et d'y croire. Plus pr\u00e9cis\u00e9ment, il est interdit de : (1) \u00c9couter attentivement et encourager l'orateur \u00e0 continuer ; (2) Prendre plaisir \u00e0 entendre l'information n\u00e9gative ; (3) Croire ce que vous avez entendu comme un fait \u00e9tabli. Le Talmud dit qu'une personne qui \u00e9coute du lashon hara est en r\u00e9alit\u00e9 pire que l'orateur, car l'orateur peut faire t\u00e9shouva en disant \u00e0 la personne dont il a parl\u00e9 qu'il a invent\u00e9 \u2014 mais l'auditeur a d\u00e9j\u00e0 re\u00e7u l'information dans son esprit et le dommage \u00e0 sa perception est fait. Implications pratiques : si quelqu'un commence \u00e0 vous dire quelque chose de n\u00e9gatif sur un tiers et que vous \u00eates coinc\u00e9 dans la conversation \u2014 vous avez deux niveaux d'obligation : (a) Essayer de rediriger ou de sortir. (b) Si vous \u00eates coinc\u00e9, d\u00e9cider consciemment de NE PAS croire ce que vous entendez. Vous pouvez \u00e9couter sans croire. Le Hafets 'Ha\u00efm appelle cela \u00ab entendre sans accepter \u00bb. Une intuition cl\u00e9 : nous sommes command\u00e9s de NE PAS croire le lashon hara \u00e0 propos d'un autre Juif \u2014 m\u00eame si nous ne pouvons pas imm\u00e9diatement le r\u00e9futer. Nous devons maintenir la pr\u00e9somption d'innocence. C'est extr\u00eamement contre-intuitif pour nos oreilles modernes, mais c'est la halacha r\u00e9elle. Source : Hafets 'Ha\u00efm, Hilchot Rechilut ; Talmud, Niddah 61a.
